commit 103ef3477753a12f9364cb6a091e30d81e6e17a3
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-10-02 13:47:48 +1100

Replaced several misuses of CvUnit::getMoves with baseMoves

There were a few places in the AI which used getMoves when they really
wanted baseMoves. The main side effect of this was that many searches
too longer than they should; but it also resulted faulty reasoning for
some decisions (eg. thinking the enemy was in range when it wasn't).

It's very frustrating for me that CvUnit::getMoves doesn't mean the same
thing as CvUnitInfo::getMoves. I'd rename one of them, but they are both
quite engrained.

commit d1f55f29aa0daeec6157ee1e2b473ef37fe7ebe0
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-30 00:54:07 +1000

Adjusted AI_counterPropose to prefer an unfair deal over no deal.

When considering the iValueForThem > iValueForUs case, we were trying to
get as close to a balanced trade as possible. However, this meant that
when the fairest deal would favour a human 'them', the AI would decline
to offer any deal at all.

I've altered the behaviour so that the top priority is to favour 'us',
and getting a fair deal is secondary; rather than the other way around.
This means fair AI-AI deals might be less likely; but counter-proposals
to human trade offers will work better. And that's the main aim.

commit 0473972f3de401e2add2f01d46d17602c034a98b

Minor tweaks to CvCityAI::AI_yieldValue.

The recent adjustments to CvCityAI::AI_updateBestBuild call

meant to be used; but I have tried to make negative values acceptable in
my previous changes. And these tweaks help improve that a bit more.

commit 00c5f169a196c36ae897f2ec595a950b4a322b64

Fixed a bug which discouraged the AI from chopping.

There was a mistake in AI_updateBestBuild which caused the final chop
condition to overrule all the other chop conditions.

I've fixed the mistake, and adjusted the code to make similar mistakes
less likely. I've also relaxed a couple of the conditions to make
chopping more likely.

commit 68bf5845c92505fdca826f6d8869a399fbead281
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-28 22:25:35 +1000

Rewrote CvPlayerAI::AI_counterPropose to get more balanced deals.

AI_counterPropose now worked by evaluating all possible trade items
before adding them to the trade, so that items can be added in the order
most likely to result in a balanced deal.

In addition to this, the AI will now be slightly more generous to humans
in the sense that the automatic counter proposals from human players
will no longer add gold if the AI would accept the deal without gold.
These automatic counter proposals are the only time the AI will allow a
discounted trade with a human. This change means that the AI may offer a
trade deal which favours a human player even if the human player has
enough gold to balance the deal. Previously, if the human player had a
lot of gold on hand, the AI would never offer a discounted trade. (Also
note that in the original BtS code, the AI would never offer a
favourable deal to a human under any circumstances.)

This was a significant rewrite, so there might be some bugs. However, my
main concern is that the new version might actually work 'too well' in
the sense that AI players might make significantly more trade deals with
each other, and thus be stronger than before. We'll see if further
changes are needed.

commit 5c862c2b2b4c6ae740e6f12940314a67e4d2257f
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-28 15:33:17 +1000

Tweaked CvPlayerAI::AI_tradeAcceptabilityThreshold

of normal to 2/3 of normal.

commit 1de57cb5957bbea8221a22f435fa16e82133bc6c
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-28 14:04:01 +1000

Improved clarity and consistency in CvPlayerAI::AI_counterPropose

Reduced the scope of temporary variables, and changed the usage of
'weight' and 'value' to be consistent.

'value' means how much the item would add to the trade deal; whereas
'weight' is an arbitrary scale used to decide which items we should
prefer to trade.

I hope that these changes will reduce the likelihood of mistakes.

commit a89741571f13732613fa1c8c69e572949f76ec4a

https://github.com/DarkLunaPhantom/Civ4-K-Mod/ Apparently work was
originally done by alberts2.

Some of the changes are my own.

commit 48fd4c01102e13acbcfe3091bdb86d97e213702e
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-28 13:10:50 +1000

Fixed some memory leaks

Fixed a few more cases where `new` was used to create an array, but
`delete[]` was not used to free it. (Sometimes `delete` was used
instead. Sometimes the function returned without freeing at all.)

To fix these problems I've started replacing dynamically allocated
arrays with std::vector, so that their destruction is handled
automatically. Ideally, `new` and `delete` should only be used inside
constructors and destructors.

CvPlayerAI::AI_techValue now takes vector arguments rather than arrays.

commit 1129c1e740652f1008762e8eab8886a4243848da
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-28 11:51:31 +1000

Fixed potential pointer invalidation in CvSelectionGroup::groupMove

The selection group can be messed up when units move. eg. If a city is
captured, the change in culture could bump the remaining units.

To get around this, CvSelectionGroup::groupMove uses a copied list of
units rather than the live list of units.

Thanks to alberts2 and DarkLunaPhantom for the tip.

commit 3f64e50e0f91c0663790103da348538d04694509

Changed some corporation maintenance.

Increased maintenance for Civilized Jewelers. Decreased maintenance for

The fact that Civ. Jewelers is unlocked so early makes it a powerful way
to boost a civilization's economy even ignoring the culture provided.
Increasing the maintenance doesn't seem like a great 'fix'; but I do

The other two corporations are in the opposite situation. They are
unlocked late in the game, and their bonuses are situatoinal anyway.

commit a603058b827f1b7b6785532ae01667915c7b061a
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-26 17:40:44 +1000

Fixed an AI bug preventing DoW with transports that ignore borders.

AI_considerDoW now checks that the whole group can enter an area; and
checks for amphibious landings.

Without this, ships such as the East Indiaman could get stuck waiting to
go to war, because they themselves could enter enemy land without war
but their cargo and escorts could not.

commit 6047432cf43a3f94b7ae5a235f137a8ad475cdf6
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-09-26 15:20:09 +1000

Fixed misuse of maxMoves() when intending baseMoves()

There were several places where CvUnit::maxMoves() was used when
baseMoves() was intended. This was mostly in old naval AI code. The main
effect of this was to increase the search time for the AI by searching
around 400 times more plots than intended.

baseMoves() is the number of tiles a unit can move. maxMoves() the total
"movement points", which is baseMoves() * a constant.

Author: karadoc <hidden>

Fixed several problems with slavery evaluation in AI_yieldValue

There were some mistakes which mean slavery was sometimes counted when
it shouldn't be, and sometimes wasn't counted when it should be; but the
biggest problem was that it was a factor of 100 too small... and so it
was essentially being ignored.

I've fixed the scale problem and adjusted the conditions.

commit 7eb1744d035556200b2d3d4df77e15a48dae34d5
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-04-01 09:38:30 +1100

Adjusted cultural revolt probability and properties.

Increased the base change of revolt from 10% to 15%. Decreased the
duration of revolts from 3+2*(previous revolts) to 2+(previous revolts).
Increased the number of 'warning revolts' from 1 to 2. ie. Cities will
now flip on the 3rd revolt rather than the 2nd.

The net effect of these changes is that the average number of turns to
flip a city will be unchanged, and the number of turns spent in revolt
will be similar to before - but the chance of each revolt is a bit
higher and so it's a bit more predictable and less dependant on luck.

commit d68b71a5895d6d4cc00d75074cc6b6952dcbeab6
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2016-05-14 23:32:45 +1000

Fixed air intercepts conflicting with combat in simultaneous turns.

Air intercept battles previous did not check if the intercepting unit
was already fighting. This could cause bad things to happen.

Also, air intercept battles no longer check if their is combat on the
intercepting unit's plot. This means that the air combot & intercept can
happen while the plot is being attacked (as long as the intercepting
unit itself is not fighting). This is a somewhat experimental change...
I can't think of any problems with it; but maybe there is something I
haven't thought of.

commit c32ec421d7c1fd0e8854da8eaee2a610530ab97b
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-09-26 13:26:57 +1000

Adjusted CvTeam::shareCounters to prevent lose of circumnavigation bonus.

There is no perfect way to share extra moves when teams merge - because
the source of extra moves is not tracked, and so we can't tell if the
two teams have the same bonuses, or independent bonuses.

I've decided to just take the maximum value of the two; which for most
cases will be correct.

commit 8b46440a9ce8d3e9107ca1836635ad9929ff7df0
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-04-02 19:18:51 +1100

estimateCollateralWeight now takes collateral resistance into account.

estimateCollateralWeight is used to approximate how much damage the AI's
collateral units will do to a stack. Until now, the calculation did not
consider collateral resistance (eg. from Drill promotions), or
collateral immunity (eg. machine-guns). Now those things are included,
roughly, in the calculations.

This means the AI is less likely to suicide its army into a well
fortified machine-gun defence.

commit 57427057b6d33b6c672f3617332b1904738031d6
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-04-02 19:14:44 +1100

Relaxed conditions in AI_retreatToCity, to fix AI indecision.

Due to special conditions applied to the unit's current plot, the AI
still preferred to move to a new city rather than stay in the current
one. Those special conditions have been removed, so that the units
retreating to a city will generally be happy to just stay where they
are.

(I've corrected similar problems in AI_retreatToCity in the past; but
this change is actually the most straight forward.)

commit f22bcf3d94cee037ff438da6272893aa3350fe25
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-04-01 22:44:40 +1100

Tided the xml used in CvGameTextMgr::setUnitHelp

CvGameTextMgr::setUnitHelp was previously using "<img=%S size=16></img>"
for all the promotion icons. I've changed it to "<img=%S size=16 />"
instead, which is a bit shorter and cleaner.

Realistically it shouldn't make any difference; but I've encountered a
rare bug which messes up the on-screen text from setUnitHelp. I've spent
quite a lot of time debugging it, and my best guess is that it is a bug
in the xml processor (which I assume is in the .exe, because I can't
find it in the dll code).

In the save game I was using to reproduce this bug, changing the img
tags to the shorter version removed the problem. I don't think the bug
is actually related to that though. I think it's something to do with
the precise length of the text or something like that - because changing
pretty much anything at all removed the problem. I'm just committing
this change as a kind of memento of the time I've spent debugging this
problem.

commit c6fb8b8bc960d4c3fcd290faa556dbc00e20ca1d
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-03-21 12:55:53 +1100

Implemented "SpecialistExtraCommerce" xml field for technologies.

Techs can now give a civ-wide commerce bonus to all specialists in the
same way that civics can. The new xml field, SpecialistExtraCommerces,
is optional - so techs which don't use this new field do not need to be
updated.

The AI has been taught to evaluate the new bonus. And the python tech
screen has been updated to show an icon and mouse-over text for techs
with the new bonus.

I've also changed the tech boxes in the research screen to be slightly
wider, so that the box for Scientific Method will be wide enough in
include one more bonus.

commit caebff59e14ca8f9810473ed0b7b0988881206e9
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-03-14 15:14:56 +1100

Adjusted pathfinding cost for exploring units.

The path cost of unrevealed terrain is now reduced for automated
explorers, and units with explore AI type.

Movement cost is not longer increased when moving from 1 unrevealed plot
to another unrevealed plot. Instead, such movement is just given a
higher pathfinding cost for no exploring units.

commit 7f7b91279162bddfa9943fd31befccb7b4db6237
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-03-08 12:35:25 +1100

Fixed bPrioritiseAirlift causing oscillations in AI_retreatToCity.

Previously, the prioritise airlift feature was only loosely enforced -
such that units would sometimes choose a close city without airlift
rather than a far city with airlift. Unfortunately this would sometimes
cause units to oscillate in and out of non-airlift cities without making
any progress.

bPrioritiseAirlift is now strictly enforced to prevent the oscillation
problem.

(I also tidied up the code a little bit.)

commit 4fa2bf46dc31ae78034c06636a05374e90fd1f84
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-03-08 10:06:42 +1100

Stopped "noCapture" from capturing cities with non-combat units.

Previously gunships could capture cities that were only defended by
non-combat units (such as workers).

"no capture" units should be able to attack workers - but not when those
workers are in undefended cites!

(Note: the rules in "canAttackOrMoveInto" are pretty messy. Perhaps one
day they should be cleaned up to be clearer.)

commit 6453e513f64ccc3927897657d0b474cddbcd44b6

commit 46c71d84e0f914d8e8159c88d884fb2183d1f391
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-02-14 18:15:45 +1100

Reduced chance of spies being caught while exploring friendly land.

The "recent mission" term in the spy intercept probability is applied if
the spy has not been fortified or if there is more than one friendly spy
on the same plot. This meant that spies exploring in friendly (foreign)
territory often got caught.

I've changed the 'recent mission' penalty so that it now only applies if
one of the following conditions are met:
 * More than one spy is on the plot.
 * The players are at war.
 * A counter-espionage mission is in effect.
 * A counter-spy (or security bureau) is on the same plot.

Roughly speaking, this means that probability of catching friendly spies
is a lot lower, but the probability of catching hostile spies is
unchanged.

commit f8cfb6db7827aa7a6d3c56f89818f405d917d527
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-02-14 18:00:28 +1100

Inflation rate now increases with global tech state.

Added function CvPlayer::updateInflationRate, and replaced
calculateInflationRate with getInflationRate. (Mods which used
calculateInflationRate in their python code will need to be updated to
use getInflationRate instead.)

Inflation is now cached for each player. (The new inflation calculation
is significantly slower than the old.) Note: saves from before this
change will have zero inflation for the first turn, due to limitations
of the load process.

The effects of inflation increase with each turn as before, but now the
'effective turn' number used in that calculation depends on how many
technologies have been discovered globally.

The goal of this change is to increase inflation in games with a high
tech-rate, so that the inflation rate is suitably high when civs have
the advantage of late-game buildings and plot improvements.

Tweaked global warming values to start a bit earlier.

Resistance reduced from 10 to 9.
Index per chance increased from 450 to 500.

I'm considering adding some kind index reduction effect to slow down
run-away warming; but I'll see how this goes first.

Land on other islands is now counted as "bad" for starting locations.

commit fe731b39de0c1a1d2a4d6a26392317bf4166b4a6
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2015-01-24 12:51:45 +1100

Capitulation power is now determined after cities are reassigned.

Vassals are able to free themselves if their land drops below some
percentage of what it was when the capitulation deal was signed.

That original land size is now determined at the end of deals rather
than at the start, so that capitulation deals which involve city
transfers don't result in vassals being able to free themselves
immediately.

(Also made some style adjustments.)

commit c11a1ba76f3b9ff04bab80395eae10f5294dbbff

commit 13536b4873e3f933131b96a29761793fa9a98fe4
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-12-09 17:45:23 +1100

Adjusted value of food in AI_yieldValue to avoid overvalue problems.

The previous value system sometimes resulting in high value plots being
left unworked because those same high value plots were causing the
growth value of other plots to be even higher value.

Essentially the problem is caused by the casual overestimating of growth
value. So to fix it, I've reduced the base growth value to a more
natural (and lower) calculation, and made some other food value
adjustments to compensate the change.

commit 0e3abf7d77ce0af927955fc1ecf8d5a92622cc07
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-12-09 17:26:17 +1100

Fixed commerce loss being ignored in AI_jobChangeValue.

The code was missing a minus sign, which caused commerce loss values to
be negative, which essentially meant they were ignored by AI_yieldValue.

I suppose the effect of this bug is that specialists would be much more
likely to be kept once they were assigned.

commit c8b2dc8f599d7b3328bb07c9984b3f5a8a4e3f79
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-12-02 23:19:00 +1100

Added gold slider estimate for use in cultural victory strategies.

Added method CvPlayerAI::AI_estimateBreakEvenGoldPercent.
AI_estimateBreakEvenGoldPercent estimates the percentage needed on the
gold slider to pay for all on-going expenses.

AI_estimateBreakEvenGoldPercent is now used for
AI_calculateCultureVictoryStage, and AI_updateCommerceWeights to provide
a more stable estimate of how many turns it would take to achieve a
cultural victory.

(I'm tempted to use AI_estimateBreakEvenGoldPercent in
AI_commerceWeight, to increase the value of gold when the civ's economy
is weak. But I'm worried that it will be a bit too slow; and that it
will be double-counting with the AI's "special yield" modifiers.)

commit d5f11bcd6f10d353065ae3455144366d0853eea2
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-12-01 11:50:47 +1100

Fixed a bug in the evaluation of food difference in AI_yieldValue.

When AI_yieldValue was used only for plots, I chose to not count growth
value for plots which did not offer any yield than citizens would
consume (eg. a grassland plot with no river and no improvements).

AI_yieldValue is now used for direct comparisons between plots, and so
we can no longer assume that a yield of only 2 food is useless - because
it might be a _difference_ of two food.

Note: the best way to restore the behaviour of ignore growth value on
bad plots would be to alter iGrowthValue in AI_plotValue.

commit 313e2ae739864fd5968c5c0de3c80487cdee6f08
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-11-21 11:40:51 +1100

Added new functions for evaluating citizen jobs.

CvCityAI::AI_jobChangeValue will supersede AI_plotValue and
AI_specialistValue. It can directly evaluate a swap from one job to
another, as well as adding and removing jobs.

AI_finalImprovementYieldDifference and AI_specialPlotImprovementValue
are helper functions for AI_jobChangeValue.

The evaluation in AI_jobChangeValue is essentially the same as the
existing evaluation in AI_plotValue and AI_specialistValue. Those older
functions will soon be changed to refer directly to AI_jobChnageValue to
avoid code duplication.

Also, AI_yieldValue is now able to accept a NULL yields vector.

NOTE: currently, AI_jobChangeValue uses AI_getGreatPersonWeight when
evaluating specialists for both human and AI players; but those weights
are not updated for human players. This may cause undesired behaviour of
someone turns autoplay on and then off again.

force count is now reduced.

commit 7d9e34dc788433a3d9ce3795bfcfe73dcedca934
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-10-25 22:20:45 +1100

Tweaked the handling of happiness and growth in AI_yieldValue.

There is a complex interplay between the approximate food-per-turn given
by iAdjustedFoodPerTurn and the approximate future happiness given by
iFutureHappy. The growth value adjustments from iFutureHappy were sometimes resulting
in some dubious plot choices (because high food plots can end up giving
lower growth value than low food plots).

Estimated future happiness now depends on a slower estimate of
food-per-turn, so that the 'future happiness' is more likely to be an
underestimate rather than an overestimate.

I've also increased the devalue rate. (i.e. decreased the value of
having very high food-per-turn.

Strengthen the conditions for deciding to replace an existing corp with

commit 300532663d710af4d2bd1ea5fde666f9eba214a7
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-10-25 17:32:50 +1100

Fixed OOS bugs in some random events.

There were a few events which involved sorting lists that had memory
dependant values in them. eg. list of (distance, city_pointer) pairs.
This meant that in some situations memory addresses were compared, which
sometimes resulted in OOS (because the memory address won't be the same
on all computers, thus the lists might have different orders).

I've changed it so that only the first member of the tuple is used to
sort the list. The memory address will be ignored, and so that should
solve the problem.

commit 0ee6ce4d3a97d30dabf323936f1cfa4842f40455
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-10-21 09:43:09 +1100

Fixed bugs and removed obsolete code in AI_assignWorkingPlots

Forced specialists were not handled correctly for shrinking cities. This
could result in too many citizens being assigned.

Removed unnecessary code for specialist assignment and reassignment -
those things are handled by AI_addBestCitizen and AI_juggleCitizens.

Note: the current handling of forced specialists in AI_addBestCitizen
and AI_juggleCitizens is not consistent. AI_addBestCitizen tries to
assign specialists in the same proportions that they are being forced,
whereas AI_juggleCitizens allows any proportions, but prioritises forced
specialist types over non-forced specialists. This inconsistency may
sometimes result in additional swaps in AI_juggleCitizens, but it isn't
a big problem.

commit 8ac07bd9c2ca2270e1797dc9b30289dc5d6aa16c

commit b83df1a91cefcee8696f32270ffc2ff02c2060ad
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-10-11 17:58:10 +1100

Adjusted culture commerce weight calculation, and added cache.

CvPlayerAI::AI_commerceWeight now uses cached value for city culture
weight. The weight calculation has been updated and moved to
CvPlayerAI::AI_updateWeights.

The new calculation ranks culture cities by estimating how many turns it
will take them to reach legendary culture. (This is a more strategically
sensible ranking than using just their current culture rate - which is
what the old calculation did.)

Cache is updated at the start of each turn.

Note: I'm just about to do a similar cache for espionage weight.

commit 181d8c9ea552889514dac6701e35ecb5cc33eeb0
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-10-11 17:02:51 +1100

Minor tweaks to espionage in CvPlayerAI::AI_doCommerce.

Espionage spending is now blocked by AI_VICTORY_CULTURE4 rather than by
AI_VICTORY_CULTURE3.

The AI will now only try to control their espionage percent if they can
also control their research percent. (Note, this has no effect with the
current xml.)

The current AI is designed to just compare the value of espionage to
research. If research isn't flexible, then espionage should be compared
to gold instead - which is effectively what will happen by default. When
the AI reaches their gold target it will choose to increase espionage
spending.

commit 54b7103f14b0122932c09624ded5bd5fb3296391
Author: karadoc <hidden>

Simplified AI's use of Great Works, and disabled obsolete code.

Removed CvUnitAI methods: AI_artistCultureVictoryMove, AI_greatWork,
and AI_doTrade. Removed CvCityAI::AI_calculateCulturePressure.

AI_doTrade was made obsolete many versions ago, and was no longer being
used. The code has now been deleted.

AI_greatWork was incompatible with the other great person actions
considered in AI_greatPersonMove. I've disabled it and replaced it with
AI_greatWorkValue and AI_doGreatWork, similar to the system used to
evaluate and execute trade missions.

AI_calculateCulturePressure was only used inside AI_greatWork. It
contained some calculation mistakes, and was not needed anywhere else,
so I've disabled it.

AI_artistCultureVictoryMove has been disabled so that great works and
super specialists can be considered in the standard way, inside
AI_greatPersonMove.

commit 35d35c66309ba3e324dcf11a50e6f09646dd1357
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-10-07 22:34:04 +1100

Further adjustments to food handling for citizen work assignment.

Rewrote the 'iStarvingAllowance' calculation in AI_yieldValue. The
previous implementation only triggered for AI players with 'avoid
growth' turned on - which was impossible. The new implementation allows
some food loss when the bar is above 80% full, both for AI and human
players (with slightly different rules).

Simplified and tweaked some of the other starvation calculations.

AI_juggleCitizens now uses "bRemove=true" for considering both worked
and unworked plots. This is a kludge. It makes more sense for bRemove to
be false when considering unworked plots. But the fact is that however
we do it is going to be somewhat unhelpful, because what we really need
is a direct food comparison between plots. I think the current code is
good enough for now, but if I become dissatisfied with it again, I need
to remember that a direct food comparison is the only way it is going to
get better!

commit d6ad0b85468577f0c4ea93988b2bf7fa06d51fee

Fixed some problems with cultural cities in the victory screen.

The cities are now grouped be team rather than by player, to match the

commit b9416a0733e02a8f03ab5a49ef5c18a7741fea06
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-09-30 12:16:01 +1000

Optimised KmodPathFinder further by using lower-level memory management

It turns out that constructing the map of FAStarNode was eating up most
of the speed gains from my previous changes. So I've decided to go all
the way down to C style memory management, rather than using vectors /
multi_arrays.

By allocating the memory directly we bypass the FAStarNode constructor
and hence save a fair bit of time.

commit c8a3e192355d699362a834544d0c130b76928027
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-09-29 18:51:46 +1000

Changed the core of KmodPathFinder to use a single block of memory.

node_map is now a multi_array<FAStarNode, 2>, and the path finder no
longer uses any shared_ptr.

This change will (usually) use a bit more memory than the previous
implementation, but I expect it to be significantly faster, because
there will be fewer memory lookups and far fewer allocations and
deallocations.

Initial testing suggests this makes the path finder around 25% faster,
but that it is still only a tiny speed boost overall. Apparently I
forgot that the path finding is no longer a large part of the total CPU
time.

commit 20ee7503a4502ea777f06fe217e0f78e8b66c83e

Simplified the move conditions in CvSelectionGroup::groupMove.

This change should have almost no effect on gameplay.

like that. Also, I've removed some redundant checks.

commit 1298739243fd7c1c9c37dfe97f987ce45bb4171f
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-09-28 10:31:27 +1000

Fixed units getting bumped when simultaneously attacking and defending.

This fixes a bug which sometimes caused units to move onto plots which
still had enemy defenders.

The root of the bug was that when two units attempt to attack each other
at the same time, the game failed to track which unit was in the process
of attacking.

I've corrected this by clearing attackPlot when a unit is defending. And
I've added some additional conditions and asserts to prevent similar
problems in the future.

commit 5b28f89dc3d5fd4c86faa91e1d505664c92404f8
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-09-16 19:44:19 +1000

Restructured pathfinder usage to not use getPathLastNode.

FAStarNode pointers returned by the pathfinder become invalid when the
pathfinder is destroyed. Because of this, I consider it bad practice to
use these pointers. In fact, the the pathfinder shouldn't allow any kind
of external access to them at all. Not only could misuse result in
segfaults, but the pointers could also be misused in a way to mess up
the internal state of the pathfinder...

So, in this patch, almost all usage of FAStarNode has been removed from
outside of the pathfinder. This will have no effect on the execution of
the game, but it may help to reduce bugs in the future.

I've disabled CvUnit::getPathLastNode and
CvSelectionGroup::getPathLastNode, and replaced their usage with new
pathfinder methods such as KmodPathFinder::GetFinalMoves and
KmodPathFinder::GetPathTurns.

There are only a couple of places where FAStarNode is still used. One is
in CvUnitAI::AI_solveBlockageProblem, which doesn't use the
KmodPathFinder, so I probably won't change it. The other is
CvUnitAI::AI_considerPathDOW. To correct this, I intend to create a new
method to give access to the completed path without exposing the
internal nodes. (But I haven't done that yet.)

I've also removed the KMOD_PATH_FINDER define and preprocessor
conditions. The original bts pathfinding code has been deleted.

commit d9c2359ff542ad31596dd4bad2b51bcff17164e7
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2014-09-15 16:47:30 +1000

The open list in KmodPathFinder is now a vector, to improve speed.

Although it seems natural to use a linked list for this, I recently
found out that linked lists are generally slower than vectors even when
deleting and inserting in the middle of the list. I did a quick
experiment to test it, and sure enough, the vector was faster.

Thanks to Bjarne Stroustrup for the tip.

Added bNoCache argument to AI_localDefenceStrength.

The bNoCache argument indicates that we shouldn't update the strength memory.

This is so that we can use AI_localDefenceStrength in asynchronous situations
- such as AI_acceptSurrender - without having to worry about strength memory
causing OOS problems.

Strength memory is still not used for human players.

Minor change for C++11 compliance.

different to allow for perfect forwarding. So I'm just using the std::pair
constructor instead.

 modern compiler anyway.)

commit a2734a5a837eef141f476ac486e8885bfcdac076
Author: karadoc <hidden>

Disabled the safe range cache.

There are a still some cases where the cache isn't completely accurate;
and although the cache does allow us to skip around half of all checks
in AI_getAnyPlotDanger, that still only saves a negligible amount of
time.

So despite the recent work I've put into improve the cache, I've decided
to disable it so that I don't have to worry about problems caused by
invalid cache.

isSafeRangeCacheValid to always return false.)

commit d7442a052c174525799a57a678b25c2af5d2e12c
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-12-23 09:58:43 +1100

Fixed the AutoPlay module disabling event handlers from other mods.

I haven't looked much at the code for the AIAutoPlay module, so
hopefully I haven't misunderstood how it is suppose to work...

It looks like AIAutoPlay overrides the event handlers for new turns and
for new cities so that popups don't appear while autoplay is running.
I've edited the overriding events so that they basically just call the
original event handlers if autoplay is not active.

It would be better to block the popups directly rather than blocking the
event handlers. The best way to do this would be to add autoplay checks
to 'onCityBuilt' in CvEventManager.py, and to 'turnChecker' in
CvTopCivs.py. But I'm not going to make those changes right now, because
I'd rather not have to add those two files to this mod for such a
trivial reason. I might do it later if there are still problems.

commit 552496b548a60f1b0a7b6d9da67fe56ccd1a1dc3

Added randomness to the AIs decision to 'cherry pick' target cities.

When not in 'total war', the AI is a bit more selective in its choice of
cities to attack. I think this works well, except that in some
circumstances it is possible for players to use this to manipulate which
city the AI targets. I've added some randomness so that the AI sometimes
disables its cherry-picking of cities so that players can't manipulate
the AI indefinitely.

commit 56fc65343a98b8e4f22a12847a5869718562418d
Author: karadoc <hidden>

Rewrote most of AI_assaultSeaTransport.

The AI will now be able to consider amphibious attack landings on
non-city plots. Previously the AI would never do this, and the fact that
it would never do it was easy for players to exploit.

commit 28e37db6553654c02d0a3e0db2a67c4dac18f799
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-12-22 15:32:48 +1100

Made some structural changes to CvPlayerAI::AI_baseBonusVal

The motivation for these changes was that I wanted to make the AI's
resource trading a bit smarter. In particular, I wanted them to not
value strategic resources as highly if they already have another
resource to fulfil the same requirements. (eg. don't value copper as
highly if they already have iron.)

Unfortunately, after writing the changes I realised that they were
likely to cause OOS problems. So I've commented out the parts of the
code that I think could cause problems - and this means there is very
little functional difference from the original code. The only reason I'm
keeping the new code at all is that I might want to use it in the future
if I ever change the cache system such that OOS is no longer a problem.

commit 57912a126a92a41b850333bc88a828f5ea80b590
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-12-22 11:11:25 +1100

Blocked the AI from considering very early wars.

The AI will no longer consider starting a new war if less than 30 turns
have past (scaled by game speed based on 'ibarbPercent'), and if there
are fewer cities globally than half of the total cities target. ie.
Number of civs * target number of cities / 2. (Generally, I expect that
the turns limit will expire before the cities target is reached - except
perhaps in advanced start games, or in games where players start with
additional settlers or something like that.)

Note that in the original BtS AI there was a convoluted set of
conditions, based around AI_STRATEGY_GET_BETTER_UNITS, which prevented
the AI from starting early wars. Quite a long time ago I changed the
conditions of that AI strategy, and one of the side effects of my change
was that it no longer prevented early wars. That was an unintended side
effect, and so I'm addressing it now.

commit 00a7f5bc3c25a4d40e4ae90fe4628128b4ade2c9
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-23 18:34:35 +1000

Players can now tell their AI allies start war preparations.

Human players can now tell their AI team members and AI vassals to start
preparing for war against a particular team. When used, the AI will
adopt WARPLAN_PREPARING_TOTAL, and when war is eventually declared this
will be changed to WARPLAN_TOTAL. There is also a diplomacy option to
tell these AI allies to cancel the war preparations.

(Note: if this feature is not used the AI will use WARPLAN_DOGPILE, as
usual. The AI cannot currently switch between different warplans once
war is declared.)

These changes includes new diplomacy options in the "let's discuss
something else screen", new text for these diplomacy options and AI
responses, and a new type of 'diplomacy event' to be handled by the DLL.

(Note: The new diplomacy text was translated by a computer, and I
haven't verified that it's correct or appropriate.)

commit fff715388f0586a035f8ca36d7467f09e71388d2
Author: karadoc <hidden>

CvTeam::canEventuallyDeclareWar is now exposed to Python.

commit 5e4dcfba6869bb058cf48e71a5dd1d4a675f2bf0
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-23 17:57:59 +1000

Adjusted CvTeamAI::AI_doWar to handle war preparations of vassals

Previously, war preparation strategies (WARPLAN_PREPARING_TOTAL /
LIMITED) were handled the same way for all teams. This doesn't make
sense for vassal teams however, as the vassal is unable to actually
declare war and so there is no sense in upgrading from
WARPLAN_PREPARING_TOTAL to WARPLAN_TOTAL. So instead this has been
changed so that vassals of human teams will have their warplans simply
time-out, and that vassals of AI teams will keep the warplans for as
long as their AI master does.

I've also made a tweak to CvTeam::declareWar so that prepare_total
becomes total when appropriate. I suspect this change will make no
difference whatsoever due to the conditions and circumstances that come
before it, but it's done now nevertheless.

(Note: currently this will have no effect, because vassals never use
those preparation warplans. However, I'm just about to implement changes
which allow players to tell their vassals to prepare for war, so it will
soon be important.)

commit cc429ce0595715d401e3ff4f8b14e7f0c226cdc7
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-22 20:52:16 +1000

Fixed a minor bug in AI_doWar relating to automatic peace deals.

The bug was that when making a peace deal, 'break' was used instead of
'continue', which meant that the AI would ignore peace conditions with
other teams after making peace with any one team.

(This was a very long-standing bug from the original BtS code and bbai
code. The bug was made more obviously visible by my style adjustments.)

commit 72c5db5bddcff5e4ea182ed75d02b20c174aae82
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-22 19:16:18 +1000

Made some style / structure adjustments to CvTeamAI::AI_doWar

Some huge 'if' blocks have been changed into 'if! continue', as is the
style I've been using in other parts of the code.

Some loop variables have been changed from ints to enums (and renamed),
for some additional type safety; CvPlayerAI references are now used in
place of GET_PLAYER in a few places.

The aim of these style adjustments is to make it easier to read the
code, to spot bugs and to implement future changes. Hopefully I didn't
make any mistakes while making these changes.

commit 25abcd0017f5e6fb92d4a6825b7e23f46c5cb064

commit 3cf6a3e5877fe683bbf36aee7bcc4de533a7edca
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-07 12:58:19 +1000

Corrected an inconsistency the move flags used in AI_greatPersonMove.

Invisible units (ie. great spies) were still using
MOVE_NO_ENEMY_TERRITORY when looking for 'slow' missions, but not when
actually executing those missions. This could create some pathfinding
inefficiency, and could potentially cause the invisible great person to
get stuck in enemy territory.

Also removed some danger / enemy unit checks. These checks shouldnt' be
applied to invisible units, and they're already handled in generatePath
anyway.

(The area check in this function is also already handled in generatePath
- but double-checking the area has become a kind of convention since
bbai erroneously decided efficiency would be improved by putting it
everywhere.)

commit 4353c288b11478e61254bc999a90842e81a8718a
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-05 16:40:45 +1000

Corrected a mistake in the final spread condition of AI_bestReligion.

The calculation of the extent that the religion has spread was using the
maximum of the target cities and the player's cities, which meant that
players with fewer cities than the target may be unable to reach the
spread requirements even if the religion was in all of their cities.

I've changed it to use the _minimum_, of
(1.5*target cities + 1, current cities + 1).

commit 16da5d4a99ecbcc6281b6796b786fb5971d7b58f
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-05 16:34:22 +1000

Fixed a rare bug in AI_cityTradeVal which could cause a seg-fault.

When evaluating bonuses, AI_cityTradeVal wasn't checking if the bonus
could be seen by the other team before evaluating what the other team
could see - and since AI_bonusVal assumes the argument isn't NO_BONUS,
this could cause a seg-fault or an unpredictable evaluation.

This bug was due to my previous changes.

commit 5066698105e728a3b95dfc00e9c02933e0cd406e

commit b12078ec5ddd2a4a0c83b2376fb2452331219073
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-07-03 18:59:40 +1000

Changed the danger interrupt condition for workers.

Originally, workers would stop if there was any danger within two steps.
Awhile back I changed this so that danger was ignored if the worker's
command was issued while the worker was already in danger. But recently
I've found that this produces some unintuitive outcomes which may cause
players to have their workers captured. I've now changed the condition
so that if the command is issued while in danger, the worker will still
be interrupted if there is danger within 1 step - but not 2 steps.

If this new version is later found to not be satisfactory, I guess I'll
have to change it again so that there are three different modes for the
workers - interrupt for 2 steps, for 1 step, or not at all - depending
on ... stuff.

commit 3085e596669cf1546c88b1b74863e66282a0e9f3

'dirty power' unhealthiness was shown.

Mouse-over text for buildings that provide power now includes power health

commit 8c8e8288a63a7be7aa66c6fea56fca64bd7b81fc
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-06-21 19:36:40 +1000

Reduced the tech value of air units and reduced the conquest multiplier

Jet fighters in particular were being overvalued. So I've removed the
special air value bonus that I'd put it when I first started changing
those values, and I've increased the value of collateral damage (ie
bombers) to compensate.

Also the value multiplier applied when using conquest or domination
victory strategies has been reduced. I've noticed that in the end game,
leading AI teams are very often using conquest 2 or higher even if their
best chance of victory is by some other means - and thus unit tech value
multiplier was directing all AI's onto war techs even when they should
be researching space techs. My change here is just minor, but hopefully
its in the right direction!

commit 4eb419149301db50fcb95297253d40a1a093adcf
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-06-21 18:00:22 +1000

Fixed two rare pathfinding bugs.

The non-uniform path code had a two minor mistakes.

Firstly, the possibility of a non-uniform cost was being ignored on the
first step of each turn (apparently I was intending to turn that into a
special case, for efficiency, but I never got around to it).

Secondly, when forward-propagating changes on a path, the path cost was
being recalculated before the parent node was updated, and so in the
path was inaccurate when tracing backwards to calculate the non-uniform
cost of the path.

These two bug only affected a sub-set of the cases that were already
affected by the original bug that the non-uniform stuff was meant to fix
anyway - so they were really very rare.

commit cb00db8e6400d8e34c5f0850933aeee4f5fbe771
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-06-18 22:14:59 +1000

Fixed another bug in the bbai danger cache, and made it more flexible.

In the bbai code, 'ActivePlayerNoDangerCache' was being set true if
there was no danger found regardless of the range being checked; and yet
this cache was being used for iRange <= DANGER_RANGE. This is a bug. For
example, the NoDangeCache might be set true after confirming that there
is no danger for iRange == 1, and then that cache could be used to
declare the plot safe for iRange == 4 regardless of what enemies might
be in that extended range.

The obvious way to fix this bug is to only set the cache to true if
iRange >= DANGER_RANGE, but I figure this would essentially remove any
performance gains from the cache - so instead I've rewritten it to be a
flexible safe range.

ActivePlayerNoDangerCache has been replaced with
ActivePlayerSafeRangeCache which signals the maximum range that is known
to be safe.

commit ed15835e4e2a931abdeb49a151d204de88931f47
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-03-15 16:13:04 +1100

Fixed a bug which caused the declare war move popup to appear twice.

When the player agrees to declare war, the war declaration and the move
command are both issued as net commands. Since the declare war popup is
now triggered when the net command is being sent - this makes the popup
trigger again before the war declaration is executed.

To fix this, I'm using the MOVE_DECLARE_WAR flag to indicate that we
shouldn't check for the popup. It's an ugly fix, and I'm sorry about
that.

commit 4657073dc18bb8ccda4adb22e514bc2a9ecc22c6
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-03-13 14:31:57 +1100

Removed the temporary compatibilty hack for the 'disorganized' promotion

When the new promotion was added, I made some ad-hoc changes to the way
save games are loaded so that the new promotion didn't break old save
games.

This change was always intended to be temporary, and I've now removed
it. Hence, the next version of K-Mod will no longer be able to load save
games from before the promotion was added.

The temporary compatibility hack worked fine for K-Mod itself, but it
could cause problems for other mods which have different xml and so on.
In general, the DLL should not have to worry about the number of
promotions in the xml. The compatibility fix was just a kludge. Perhaps
in some later version I'll try to improve the save game format so that
such kludges are unnecessary.

commit dcfd9d8ad6dcba9cada1a4a4e104ca7a9a1cef0c
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-02-22 16:33:20 +1100

Corrected a problem which caused XML comments to break in some places.

There were several places in the XML loading process which tried to jump
to a child node without first skipping the comments. Because of this,
XML comments inside 'array' XML elements would cause the XML to fail to
load.

commit f0ed66a0d529b0b2a9cd186d75a44d10587613de
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-02-05 18:33:49 +1100

Moved some of the AI_buildingValue veto conditions to fix a cache bug.

There are some conditions which cause AI_buildingValue to return zero.
However, in certain situations these conditions were being bypassed when
the building value cache was already set.

For example, if the city evaluated a non-wonder building and cached the
value, then later on tried to evaluate the building again with the
BUILDINGFOCUS_WORLDWONDER flag, the flag would be ignored because the
cached value would be used before the flag was checked.

This problem is now fixed. (But I'm also going to fix it in another way
in the next commit.)

now...

commit df7c7f9a675cedf4d4b3f37eaabcee20701f3d2a
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-01-27 10:56:43 +1100

Made changes & fixes to the evaluation of starting positions.

Fixed a couple of problems in the original BtS handling of starting
positions which prevented the foundValue function from correctly
identifying existing starting positions. (eg. getMinOriginalStartDist
did not ignore it's own plot; and isStartingPlot did not count
dynamically chosen starting plots.)

Added some factors to the starting position evaluation to adjust for the
number of resources in the area, and the number of players already
placed in the area. The goal is to encourage players to be placed on the
most bountiful areas, and to reduce the likelyhood of isolated starts.

Fixed a bug which caused starting resource to be valued more highly than
intended.

Made a couple of other tweaks the the starting position evaluation.

Deleted some whitespace.

commit 3af7f7fd6a9ff29e7c0faf415bebfe7e951e6397
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-01-26 14:14:30 +1100

Fixed an int overflow problem in CvPlayerAI::AI_foundValue_bulk

For starting locations, the original BtS code included a large factor
for precision, which very frequently caused the int value to overflow -
meaning that starting locations were often evaluated incorrectly.

I've removed this factor, and added some additional checks at the end of
the function to (hopefully) detect similar problems in the future.

commit f1d2f3d153e121adf82d2d181d2dca38a6254707
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2013-01-23 17:45:29 +1100

Reversed the effect of bPrereqReligion for units and buildings.

Previously, if bPrereqReligion actually meant that a religion must _not_
be present in order to construct the building/unit. This is
counter-intuitive, and so I'd guess it was a mistake. bPrereqReligion
now means that a religion is required. (Thanks to sjodster for pointing
this out.)

Note: this change has no effect with the current xml, because
bPrereqReligion is zero for all units and buildings anyway.

commit 89c902c322270c5b3a7789dc34a8bebc91855e8e
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-12-17 18:16:37 +1100

Fixed a BtS pathfinding bug which caused inaccurate path turns.

Previously, if units with different speeds were grouped together moved with different movement costs, the pathfinder would fail to calculate the correct number of path turns. The most obvious example is when moving a group with mixed speeds along a railroad.

The bug was caused by the fact that the path nodes only store the lowest
moves value for the group, and so if the unit with more moves also has a
greater move cost, then the pathfinder will effectively be using the
lower moves with the higher movement cost.

I've fixed this by recalcuating the exact number of move for each unit
for the final turn of the path whenever there are mixed movement costs
involved. I expect this to have negligible speed inpact.

--

Also, I've changed CvSelectionGroup::maxMoves to be the minimum of the
group's max moves rather than the maximum. This seems far more sensible
to me.

commit 8e37b0ad1caaa4b7db1a8e8ec4ac55912be19d02
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-12-17 11:22:37 +1100

Rescaled and adjusted AI_warDiplomacyCost.

The previous version had some strange scaling based on population, which
had some counter-intuitive effects. (I'm not sure why I'd used that
scaling, and I'd even commented in the code that it was strange.) The
new scaling is based on the default number of players for the map size.

I've also made some adjustments to the weight. In general, the effect of
the team's "peace weight" has been dramatically reduced. (I did some
rough calculations and decided that the effect of peace weight was...
huge.)

I'd like some case data to get a sense of how well this function is
working, but I don't really want to test it right now...

gifted unit, and the AI player's current military needs. (In general,

worth a lot if the AI is losing a war.)

commit 31e0cd7a73b41bc20e7ee26dec88a51fbf208418

Made some adjustments to CvGameTextMgr::buildBuildingRequiresString

For buildings such as catherals which require a number of other

of (catheral style) buildings currently under construction. This means
if a catheral cannot be added to the build queue of multiple cities due

number of temples required.

the what buildings the current player happens to have.

Cleaned up the style of some of the code to be more maintainable.

commit 92c11f21d7ebad882f95130706145155fb4f4b28
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-11-17 17:09:13 +1100

Research is now completely halted while in anarchy.

Previously, research would continue as normal while in anarchy. The
commerce rate would be zero, but the civ would still get the 'base
research' points (which is set to 1 in the default xml). Now, research
is completely halted during anarchy, including the free base research.

The primary reason for this change is not really a good one... the
reason is that the AI cannot evaluate techs accurate while in anarchy,
and so I don't want them to have to choose their research while in
anarchy.

I've also changed a couple of things related to the triggering of
choose-research popups.

commit edf7e424a0e247cadb1aa167e092417819a3dab1
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-11-17 12:25:49 +1100

CvPlayer::canTrain team/national limits are now skipped if bTestVisible

The global unit limits are enforced based on the number of units ever
built, but team limits and national limits are based on the number of
units currently active. So even though the units may be currently maxed
out, they won't necesearily be like that forever - and therefore they
should still be visible.

commit 16233059bc8499691adbdbb9878ba9d28bf15389
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-11-16 17:05:56 +1100

Changed the odds formula for short-circuit 2&3 in AI_chooseProduction.

The new formula is more sensitive to iBuildUnitProb. My intention is
that this should put a bit more of the leader's flavour back into the
number of units built, and also it should slightly decrease the rate of
military cities getting side-tracked by other infrastructure.

Overall, short-circuit 2 will be slightly less common than before.

The threshold for short-circuit 3 has been raised, so that it will catch
fewer buildings.

Reduced the effect of pre-existing progress in AI_chooseBuilding.

Previously any pre-existing progress on the chosen building would
effectively boost the probability up to 100%. Now, the probability is
increased by progress / total cost.

Also, cleared out some bbai comments and clarified what was actually
added by bbai in a couple of places.

value and the building's flavour value, rather than the product of those
two values.

flavour as well as for defence buildings).

Made some more adjustments (ie. massive reductions) to the building

highly than the value of giving power outright. (This evaluation is

Fixed a culture problem which caused the AI to waste great engineers.

The value bonus for the initial city culture is no longer applied to
wonders or special buildings. I didn't think this would matter, because
there are other mechanisms for blocking the construction of wonders in
these situations; but I recently discovered that those mechanisms are
bypassed when the AI is deciding whether to rush a wonder with a great
engineer...

Also, reduced the priority factor for first-culture buldings.

commit ba1a42f555d2b002543ff9481d0c4e0ebbbf482f
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-10-31 15:04:55 +1100

Made lots of changes to CvCityAI::AI_cityThreat.

The threat value calculation for each player is now broken down into two
factors: iAccessFactor and iCivFactor. iAccessFactor now includes a
(very rough) naval assault calculation. Some adjustments related to
iCivFactor have been tweaked.

Also, at the end of the calculation there is now a iImportanceFactor
calculation which multiplies the total threat level based on special
factors for this city. eg. cities that are vital parts of the civ's
victory strategy are considered to be very important, and civs with
active world wonders have some added importance.

religion is in. Also, the average commerce multiplier is applied (rather
than no multiplier at all).

commit 0f1551160c3a099913333121ea2882a9ad1f3b77
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-10-23 14:53:03 +1100

Implemented an all new version of CvPlayerAI::AI_techBuildingValue.

The new function uses CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue to estimate the value
of each building in a subset of the player's cities. This value is
scaled based on the production cost of the building, and a few other
factors.

The old version of AI_techBuildingValue has been renamed to
AI_techBuildingValue_old and left intact for comparison purposes. It
will be removed at some later time.

(The following comment currently appears in the source code.)

--
The original code had some vague / ad-hoc calculations to evalute the
buildings enabled by techs. It was completely separate from
CvCity::AI_buildingValue, and it ignored _most_ building functionality.
I've decided it would be better to use the thorough calculations already
present in AI_buildingValue. This should make the AI a bit smarter, and
the code more easy to update. But it might run slightly slower.

Note: There are some cases where this new kind of evaluation is
significantly flawed. For example, Assembly Line enables factories and
coal power plants; since these two buildings are highly dependant on one
another, their individual evaluation will greatly undervalue them.
Another example: catherals can't be built in every city, but this
function will evaluate them as if they could, thus overvaluing them. But
still, the original code was far worse - so I think I'll just tolerate
such flaws for now.
--

commit 89d942d0765767820b3820daab66fd53b9754db9
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-09-24 15:23:52 +1000

Redesigned the evaluation of attack_city units.

The previous system was focus around a somewhat artibrary global target
bombard rate. The value of bombard units was boosted significantly while
below the target. Unfortunately, if siege units were powerful enough to
be chosen even when above the bombard target, then the AI would end up
with too many siege units - and also, the calculation of total bombard
was only a rough approximation, distrorted by the presence of defensive
units with bombard.

The new system does not use a bombard target, and instead focuses on the
number of units with a combat-limit of less than 100. The value of the
unit is reduced if there are already too many combat-limited units. The
reduction in value primarily targets the bombard component and the
collateral damage component.

The new system is still a bit of an ugly kludge, but I think it will
have fewer systematic weaknesses than the old system.

commit 94d44a04a0fdbda410176833ae4e411002f2d8b7

Made some changes to how data is merged when two teams merge.

changes.

maximum value, rather than just the value from the first team.

Partially reseached techs now use the sum of the research from each team
rather than just the maximum.

commit d4f66f3c9ef4997e9825d51f0f35b35a02bb839c
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-09-23 22:51:36 +1000

The trade value of techs is now independant of team size.

Usually, the trade value of a tech is proportional to its cost. The cost
of techs is proportional to the number of civs on the team; and I think
that including this team-size multiplier for trade was unfair and
counter-intuitive.

commit 49a08d907edcc3e014da3edcbbca5a34adf933d0
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-09-16 15:25:23 +1000

Reworked the tech-cost modifier for team games.

Tech cost is now directly proportional to the number of civs in the
team, but there is now a global tech cost reduction for games which
start with fewer than the default number of teams for the given world
size.

The combination of these two changes should give roughly the same tech
costs as before for games with evenly sized teams, but for games with
uneven teams the cost will be higher for the bigger teams.

commit d29ee421fd423cdd3fe6e879799df77e3c80e1b1
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-09-15 13:13:39 +1000

Made some adjustments to the AI's bombard target when evaluating units

The bombard target affects the unit evaluation when choosing which unit
to train for UNITAI_ATTACK_CITY.

This target now depends on the sum of both 'attack' and 'attack city'
units (rather than just 'attack city'); it is no longer increased for
the 'crush' strategy; it is now decreased if all of the (potential)
fighting is overseas; and the total value of the bombard rate is no
longer increased for units which ignore building defences. (If the siege
unit ignore building defences, then the non-siege units probably do as
well, and so it isn't really of any additional value.)

This bombard evaluation may need some further tweaking after this
change.

commit a69e79029c3b8ad6c4490ac72cb59d1f4aa6763e
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-19 00:37:35 +1000

Fixed some bugs which sometimes caused confusion in the sea-settler AI.

The found values for unrevelead plots is not calculated; but there was
some old AI code which sometimes made use of those found value anyway,
which could cause the AI to target very bad settling sites.

The AI will now only consider landing in areas it has explored and
identified at least one city site in. Also, the found value of
unrevealed plots is now set to zero - so that junk values can't be
accidentally used by other bits of the AI.

commit 520761b97d0d21f2b8030afc83dff25465b3401b
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-19 00:14:00 +1000

CvPlayer::addSelectionGroup now also adds the group the the cycle list.

If a selection a non-empty selection group is not in the group cycle
list, it can cause problems. In particular, it can cause the game to
hang.

There are a bunch of places in the code which will add new groups the
cycle list in particular situations... but every so often, I change
something which may create some new fringe case or something which
causes the group not to be added to the list. So now, I'm cutting the
problem off at the source. Every time a new group is created, it is
immediately added to the cycle list. It's particular position in the
cycle list can be updated at a later time.

commit cbce755ba20d0e940698d02a9eeb1e775d22300e
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-14 01:04:24 +1000

Increased the min elapsed turns for the circumnavigation bonus.

The circumnavigation bonus is only granted if the circumnavigation does
not occur on the first turn of the game. This is so that games which
start with a complete map don't give an unfair advantage to player #1.

Since CvTeam::doTurn is now called after the game turn is incremented,
the circumnatigation min-turn needed to be increased from > 0 to > 1.

commit cdc39b892959f9601fbf4f502ab379188099f107
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-13 21:18:10 +1000

ctrl/alt select will no long ignore moves when unit is already selected.

When selecting a group of units by holding ctrl/alt, if the clicked unit
is already selected then only units with moves will be selected in the
new group.

This new condition is because we can't tell the difference between a
click on the map and a click on the unit icon; and because of this, the
'ignore moves' rule can make it a bit difficult to select moveable units
when a unit without moves is already selected.

commit 5ed70f2e640a498faec0c50753ddc88b5167291d

Tweaked the sort order in the revised AI_findXRank functions.

This is now fixed.

commit 8be9088d15ac9f4004a245ad580463a49ba2958e
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-05 17:24:28 +1000

Rewrote CvCityAI::AI_getYieldMultipliers; fixed a food scaling problem.

The new version of AI_getYieldMultipliers is similar to old, but it is a
bit simplier, it includes a few flavour adjustments; but most
importantly, the food value multiplier now scales up as other yields
become more valued. This is to avoid the problem where production can
end up being worth more than the food that is necessary to work the
production.

Some other related CvCityAI functions have been tweaked to be consistent
with the new version of AI_getYieldMultipliers.

commit 26754a44823d8188aa91e3f3053b6f2baab7fe19
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-05 16:41:03 +1000

The CvCity::findXRank functions now update rank for all cities at once.

This includes findPopulationRank, findBaseYieldRateRank,
findYieldRateRank, and findCommerceRateRank.

In the original BtS code, these functions would compare the current city
to every other city to find its rank, and thus only set the cache for
the city being queried. The new code gathers all of the city data, sorts
it, and set the rank cache for every city in one pass.

commit 7afc7dc16f392cf706a8825c0dd67dbf21ccd6fe

Fixed a possible crash in AI_warCommitmentCost and changed overseas cost

AI_warCommitmentCost would previously divide by zero when evaluating an
overseas war in which neither was able to build any boats. This has been
corrected.

Also, the flat adjustement of 5/4 for total war overseas has been
replaced by a factor which depends on the relative strength of the
ground forces.

commit 354b621fa170a8c28448826f6be6503fffb82162
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-05 13:44:39 +1000

AI_getYieldWithBuild now counts yield from existing improvements.

Previously AI_getYieldWithBuild would only count yield from improvements
created by the build itself. And so, for example, if you were building a
railroad on a mine, the functino would count the natural yield of the
plot, and the extra yield from the railroad, but not from the mine
itself.

This is now corrected.

commit 5c447069c348b95a1604992cc6376388f6f6355f
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-04 12:25:39 +1000

Made some stop-gap adjustments to the AI's improvement yield evaluations

There are some serious flaws in the AI's evaluation of yield when
choosing which improvements to build. In particular, the value of food
does not scale when the value of jobs that could be worked with more
food; and the value of yield in general is inconistent with the way the
AI chooses which plots to work.. And so sometimes the AI will replace
good improvements with new ones which won't be worked; or replace high
food improvements with other improvements which won't have enough food
to be worked...

I don't address the core of these problem in this minor update, but I
have made a few changes with might help. In particular, I've decreased
the multiplier used for production, so that production doesn't end up
being worth signficantly more than food.

commit 322e8c9da1c997a57780bfe21043ed5351579814
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-03 13:58:21 +1000

Added function AI_getAvailableIncome. Replaced old code for consistency.

AI_updateAvailableIncome calculates and caches an estimate of the total
gold-per-turn revenue the player could achieve if they used 100% gold on
the commerce slider. This function is called once per turn, and the
result is accessed with AI_getAvailableIncome.

AI_getAvailableIncome is now used to replace some previous income
estimates which typically worked by simply adding
getCommerceRate(COMMERCE_SCIENCE) + getCommerceRate(COMMERCE_GOLD) + std::max(0, goldPerTurn())
The old calculation was flawed in that it failed to correctly handle
espionage or culture on the commerce slider.

commit b8f96f9b4611e08b6979859811e36959bc66cea4

that AI_commerceWeight really wanted was calculateGoldRate.

it makes sense!)

commit f27e17cfd663087d21309bd4bf0e9029e3d840d3
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-01 19:51:08 +1000

Made some adjustments to the AI's decision making for chopping forests.

The yield produced from chopping is no longer counted in the evaluation
of improvements. This allows us to decide whether or not the new
improvement would be better regardless of potential immediate benefits.

The bChop checks will now be bypassed if the city is building a process.

The value of chopping is now scaled up a bit if the player hasn't yet
reached the target number of cities for the map size.

commit 80de8b79849beacf49b804f2b1ee5efd33344b27
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-08-01 19:42:11 +1000

Made some change to how city names are choosen.

When a new city is created, and a name is being chosen from the
civilization's city name list, the search will now skip a name of names
corresponding to the number of cities the player has already founded.
This means that if a player renames a city that they have founded, the
game won't immediately suggest the same previous name for the next city.

Note 1: this only applies to names taken from the civilization city names
list. It does not apply to names on the player-specific city list which
may be used by some mods.
Note 2: previously used names will again
be suggested if the civ's city name list is otherwise exhausted.

Also, if the civilization's list of city names is exhausted, then the
game will suggest a _random_ name from a random civ; rather than the
first available city name from a random civ.

commit 49b250e819f326a633a9bb12be5f4be8f1978082
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-07-29 12:19:57 +1000

Added an avenue for the AI to use to free itself as a vassal.

CvPlayerAI::AI_considerOffer now checks the for denial of existing
vassal deals and returns 'false' if the deal would be denied.

Before this change, AI vassals would never free themselves!

(Note: on closer examination, in the original BtS code, vassals could
free themselves from AI masters but not from human masters, because of
an inconsistence in the way existing deals were being checked. So when I
changed the code to be consistent, I had unintentially taken away the
AI's avenue for canceling vassal deals with anyone at all. Now it is
fixed and better than ever.)

Also, when considering capitualion, the AI will no longer be quite so
afraid of the new master's other enemies. (ie. if the would-be master is
much stronger than the other teams they are at war with, then the
would-be vassal will not use 'we're afraid of your enemies' as an excuse
to refuse capituation.)

commit 04bf601f97534921dc5573335027c7e0d9c6a467
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-07-28 10:04:59 +1000

Removed BBAI function CvTeam::getCurrentMasterPower. Tidied some code.

CvTeam::getCurrentMasterPower was typcially used like this:
    int iPower = isAVassal() ? getCurrentMasterPower() : getPower();
This is cumbersome, and ineffecient because it has to do a vassal check
on all teams for isAVassal, and for getCurrentMasterPower.

The following code gives the same result:
    int iPower = GET_TEAM(getMasterTeam()).getPower();

Also, there could be some confusion between 'getCurrentMasterPower'
and 'getMasterPower', which are completely different functions with
completely different purposes.

So I've deleted CvTeam::getCurrentMasterPower.

automoves when shift is released.

commit f0524f55aed16ad27a2a2b18c73da176646cce28
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-07-19 14:14:27 +1000

Many bug fixes and consistency fixes related to vassals and war.

Added new function, CvTeam::getMasterTeam. For vassals, this returns the
master's team id; otherwise it returns the team's own ID.

Fixed a problem in AI_warCommitmentCost, AI_startWarVal, and
getDefensivePower, which caused defensive pacts with the target team's
master to be ignored.

Corrected some denial types in AI_vassalTrade. It no longer checks for
PEACE_NOT_POSSIBLE_US; and instead checks for WAR_NOT_POSSIBLE_US. Also,
it will now return ATTITUDE_THEM if the would-be master would refuse to
plan war, or be bought into a war, against teams that the would-be
vassal is at war with.

Restored the check for PEACE_NOT_POSSIBLE_US in AI_surrenderTrade, with
the condition that it is not checked for peace-vassal deals.

When considering starting a war with a vassal, the AI will now use the
maximum of AI_noWarAttitudeProb of the target and of the master.
(Previously it only used the target's.)

AI_warCommitmentCost now uses the target team's master for most of the
calculations, including best units, productivity estimates. Also, it now
counts war weariness due to vassals and siblings of the target, as well
as from the target itself.

for both.)

CvSelectionGroup::startMission use to set the group's activity to either
'hold' or 'mission' before checking whether the mission was possible. It
now checks the mission first, and if canStartMission returns false, the
mission is deleted without the group's activity being changed.

With this change, fortified AI groups will no longer refortify if the
fortify mission is pushed again.

(Note: unfortunately it also means that fortified AI groups will ignore
other 'wait' missions as well, including heal and sentry. But I don't
think that will make any difference for the time being.)

commit 5348a1d503b3df09f7377b090c795868828dd9e1
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-07-13 15:37:06 +1000

Reshaped the meaning of isForceUpdate.

CvSelectionGroup::readyToMove now considers isForceUpdate to be
equivalent to being awake with no missions queued.

Disabled CvSelectionGroup::doForceUpdate. Inlined setForceUpdate and
isForceUpdate.

'force update' no longer wakes sleeping units. The AI's sleeping units
are also not woken at the start of the turn. doForceUpdate is now simply
used to signal that the AI update function for each group should run at
least once per turn, regardless of whether the unit is awake or not.

AI_cancelGroupAttack and clearMissionQueue are now called explicitly
without being directly associated with force update.

With these changes, the AI can now use MISSIONS_FORTIFY if it wants.

commit d347386cd4e5efc6f4b12b9456983d8507166596
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-07-07 16:08:03 +1000

'Retire' and 'WorldBuilder' controls now always require confirmation.

Previously, doControl(CONTROL_RETIRE) would immediately execute the
retire functionalty with no confirmation. Selecting 'Retire' from the
main menu had an explicitly created confirmation popup.

In the new system, doControl(CONTROL_RETIRE) creates the confirmation
popup itself, and then the confirmation popup can call a new function
called CvGame::retire.

This means that retiring will require confirmation regardless of whether
the command came from the main menu or not and it will no require any
additional ad-hoc code. The 'WorldBuilder' command has be changed in a
similar way.

Also, the buttons in all confirmation popups now describe the action
that is to be confirmed. eg. if the action is 'retire', the buttons will
read "Retire" / "Cancel", rather than "Yes" / "No".

commit 1acc3942d453d47477cfd81c14fe6cb412ab3af8
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-07-05 12:50:00 +1000

Rewrote CvMap::updateCenterUnit to only update plots in a certain range.

Previously, CvMap::updateCenterUnit updated the center unit for every
plot on the map. This is quite an expensive thing to do; and it caused a
noticeable delay when selecting units on a big map. The new version only
updates the plots which could potentially be in movement range of the
units being selected. The range in determined using a new static
function: KmodPathFinder::MinimumStepCost.

commit 959bf1ce715cba8ee7098737b3a1adbdf3b6481a
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-06-30 14:36:15 +1000

CvTeam::doTurn is now always called at the start of the team's turn.

Previously it was called at the end of the team's turn in
non-simultaneous turns mode. But it occurs to me that if it is called at
the end of the turn, then counters such as the counter-espionage turn
counter will not work as expected. Consider, for example,
counter-espionage for 1 turn. If doTurn is called at the end of the
turn, that 1 turn of counter-espionage will end before the other
player's turn even starts.

commit bd52939528a602444fc2f569e257def61dd84fad

Changed the close-border attitude cache system.

The original close-border attitude cache system was prone to the same
OOS problems as the CAR mod cache system. So I have rewritten it using
the same, more robust, style as the new cache system.

ie. The cache is updated rigidly at the start of each turn rather than
being updated when it is first called upon.

commit 67ad94aa6b6c344f30cf053e72d96694178db695

commit 575791c4b1c2a55aa2092133f2790f6213d1fbad
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-06-21 10:21:54 +1000

Completely rewrote the attitude cache system.

Cache is now recalculated on the spot when something happens to
invalidate it.

CvPlayerAI::AI_invalidateAttitudeCache has been removed and repalced
with CvPlayerAI::AI_updateAttitudeCache.

The original system (from the 'CAR' mod) was hideously prone to OOS
bugs. I'd fixed many of the bugs in the past, but there were still more,
and it was extremely difficult to write robust code using that system.
(Here a couple of lingering bug examples from the old system.
CvTeam::declareWar didn't clear cache for the friends of the war target.
CvTeam::signDefensivePact didn't clear cache for the rivals of each
team. The crux of the problem is that in the CAR system, it was the
programmers responsibility to know exactly how and when attitude could
be affected in any way, and then clear the cache when it was affected.
If the programmer overlooked anything, it could cause OOS.)

The new system is more rigid in when the cache is recalculated; and so
similar 'bugs' will now no longer result in OOS. At worst they will
result in out-of-date attitude ratings. In fact, this is such a minor
effect that I've deliberately removed the cache update from a few places
where I think it is unimportant.

commit b46098c1a9a626e3fc1dfd81ab3c978ef86f94e8
Author: karadoc <hidden>

Fixed a bug in the iFoodBonus count in CvGame::normalizeAddFoodBonuses.

This bug essentially negated my bugfix for the plains cow problem.

Previously, I was using CvPlot::calculateMaxYield to determine which
land bonuses should count as high food plots. But I discovered today
that calculateMaxYield does not work as I expected.

I've rewritten the section in CvGame::normalizeAddFoodBonuses to avoid
using CvPlot::calculateMaxYield. And also, I've commented out the code
for CvPlot::calculateMaxYield so that it isn't mistakenly used in the
future before it is fixed.

commit 3b2066831b96ac5eeb5efb6f9391afc2dc33d0bd
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-06-14 17:55:59 +1000

First draft of my rewrite of the AI war evaluation routines.

Added new functions: CvTeamAI::AI_warSpoilsValue, AI_warCommitmentCost,
and AI_warDiplomacyCost. These functions are used to evaluate various
aspects of war. Spoils value is an estimate of what could be gained by
winning the war. Commitment cost is an estimate of how much resources
would need to be devoted toward the war. Diplomacy cost is an estimate
of how much a DoW would hurt the player's diplomatic standings.

CvTeamAI::AI_startWarVal now relies solely on these 3 new functions.
CvTeamAI::AI_endWarVal is currently unchanged, but I will probably later
rework it to use the new functions as well.

commit 0ba3b7904ed2bc55cc891dd6b43a7d0bc4e899ee
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-05-15 01:19:48 +1000

Rewrote some sections related to the loading of game text xml.
The format of the xml is now more intuitive and less rigid. In particular, the language names used to tag the xml values are now what determines the text for any given language. The order of the languages is no longer important (except in CIV4GameText_Misc1.xml, which is used to determine the correct tag names). If there is a missing language, the first text will be used (usually english). The mod can include languages from all localizations of Civ4, not just the version I happen to be using.

Changed groupCycleDistance so that it checks the actual order of units on the plot rather than using 'isBeforeUnitCycle' to decide which unit should come first.
The reason for this is that units on the plot can get out of order in some situations; and when this happens, it is better if the group cycle order matches the order on the plot rather than the ideal order.

commit 0315c6343ebb3bada6fec8e727241a0d8d09a8cc
Author: karadoc <hidden>
Date:   2012-03-23 11:10:34 +1100

Added a new argument, bAssumeVisible, to CvUnit::canMoveInto and its sister functions.
 - Previously, canMoveInto checked plot visibility for human players but not for AI players. Now it will check visibility iff !bAssumeVisible.
Added a new movement flag, MOVE_ASSUME_VISIBLE. This flag is set when the next step towards the target plot would take us backwards. When it is set, bAssumeVisible is used. (Note: bAssumeVisible is always used for AI players regardless of this flag.)
These changes fix the problem of human units forgetting that the path to their destination is blocked by an enemy unit as they lose sight of the enemy unit.

Deleted some obsolete code.
